  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_025d5342-3aed-45cb-8462-4cf2762bc9ba'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };

      initAppleId();
    } else {
      initializeSiwa();

And when the Alerans are cut off from their ships, they find themselves with no choice but to fight shoulder to shoulder if they are to survive.<br /><br /> For a thousand years, Alera and her furies have withstood every enemy, and survived every foe.<br /><br /> The thousand years are over…</span>

<div id="review_2315378667" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2315378667" />
    <a title="Mario the lone bookwolf (semi reviewing hiatus ) " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/78485297-mario-the-lone-bookwolf-semi-reviewing-hiatus"><img alt="Mario the lone bookwolf (semi reviewing hiatus ) " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1588320656p2/78485297.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2315378667?book_show_action=true">Mar 03, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mario the lone bookwolf (semi reviewing hiatus ) " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mario the lone bookwolf (semi reviewing hiatus ) " href="/user/show/78485297-mario-the-lone-bookwolf-semi-reviewing-hiatus">Mario the lone bookwolf (semi reviewing hiatus ) </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/78485297-mario-the-lone-bookwolf-semi-reviewing-hiatus?shelf=butcher-jim">butcher-jim</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2315378667" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1405458740507841617">Did I already fanboy about the Vord, an evil species I´ve already encountered in many Sci-Fi settings and that give the stereotypical „one evil emperor rules them all“ setting a fresh, new look? Often, there is any kind of control over minions with willpower, psi-tech, dark energy, that is directly linked to the power of the dictator, a dark source, sacrificing victims,… and the similarities between Sci-Fi and Fantasy are big.<br/><br/>In Fantasy, it´s always something metaphysical that is powered externa</span>
  <span id="freeText1405458740507841617" style="display:none">Did I already fanboy about the Vord, an evil species I´ve already encountered in many Sci-Fi settings and that give the stereotypical „one evil emperor rules them all“ setting a fresh, new look? Often, there is any kind of control over minions with willpower, psi-tech, dark energy, that is directly linked to the power of the dictator, a dark source, sacrificing victims,… and the similarities between Sci-Fi and Fantasy are big.<br /><br />In Fantasy, it´s always something metaphysical that is powered externally or internally or both, for instance the genetic predisposition of the chosen one described in an old prophecy who controls anything using his mindfulness and inner powers. Or hate. For external power feeding, the god emperor needs land, minions, victims, commodities, temples, power of faith of as many enslaved and forced to pray as possible, etc. I don´t know if it´s also necessary that they truly believe or just do as if. The third combination is a kind of renewable energy mix of both, the mad magician who has some concentrated power in his amulets or his battery wand or anywhere, some places with magical powers, glowing minerals, and the life energy of minions or victims. But it´s all, scientifically speaking, highly speculative bad science and fringe science.<br /><br />In Sci-Fi, there is a speculative, unproven, rea-life theoretical concept or a theory about something including quanta, other worlds, clarketech, multiverse, time travel,… that links the magic abilities with reality, gives it a better explanation than that the witch is witchy, and is often described in very detail. <br /><br />So we are coming closer to the end of this series that is getting better and better and can be easily entered with each novel (except the spoilers of course), so why not give it a try? It´s totally worth it.<br /><br />Tropes show how literature is conceptualized and created and which mixture of elements makes works and genres unique: <br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://tvtropes.org/pmwiki/pmwiki.php/Creator/JimButcher">https://tvtropes.org/pmwiki/pmwiki.ph...</a><br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://tvtropes.org/pmwiki/pmwiki.php/Literature/CodexAlera">https://tvtropes.org/pmwiki/pmwiki.ph...</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="1405458740507841617" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2147582250" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2147582250" />
    <a title="Anne" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1720620-anne"><img alt="Anne" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1415374035p2/1720620.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2147582250?book_show_action=true">Oct 26, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Anne" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Anne" href="/user/show/1720620-anne">Anne</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1720620-anne?shelf=jim-butcher">jim-butcher</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1720620-anne?shelf=read-in-2017">read-in-2017</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1720620-anne?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2147582250" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4254329554960688839">3.5 stars<br/><br/>I liked this one quite a bit more than the last book, <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2143842126' rel='nofollow noopener'>Captain's Fury</a> because there just wasn't quite as much plodding around in forests and swamps while the action happened elsewhere.<br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1509029193ra/24282527.gif' width='340' height='230' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>The majority of the story is about Tavi & Co. taking their frenemy Varg and his troops back to the Canim continent, and trying to help them take on the Vord. I don't want to give anything away -<b>unlike these fucking book titles</b> - but Tavi continues to do all the things that made me originally love him. Natur</span>
  <span id="freeText4254329554960688839" style="display:none">3.5 stars<br><br>I liked this one quite a bit more than the last book, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2143842126" rel="nofollow noopener">Captain's Fury</a> because there just wasn't quite as much plodding around in forests and swamps while the action happened elsewhere.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1509029193ra/24282527.gif" width="340" height="230" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>The majority of the story is about Tavi &amp; Co. taking their frenemy Varg and his troops back to the Canim continent, and trying to help them take on the Vord. I don't want to give anything away -<b>unlike these fucking book titles</b> - but Tavi continues to do all the things that made me originally love him. Naturally, his intelligence, courage, and goodness help him collect even more allies by the time this one is over. He's one of the most cheer-worthy heroes I've read about in a long time, and I love that Butcher created such a likable character to star in this series. It's nice to see that good guys don't always finish last!<br>I mean, is there <i>anything</i> Tavi can't do when he puts his mind to it?!<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1509030645ra/24285387.gif" width="400" height="180" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Ok, now last time around, I whined a bit about Bernard and Amara being the most <i>boring</i> couple on the planet to read about. So when they were showed up <i>again</i>, and were sent on a mission by Gaius <i>again</i>, which meant more page time spent questing with them <i>again</i>...?<br><b>I felt a tad disappointed. <i>Again.</i></b><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1509031170ra/24285716.gif" width="400" height="180" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>And while I didn't particularly enjoy reading about the first part of their journey, they pulled a nice little twist on me at the end that made it all worthwhile.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1509034559ra/24286026.gif" width="400" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Oh! And speaking of <i>twists</i>!<br>Isana learns some stuff that turns something that (I thought) was set in stone on its head. It makes a bad guy look like, well, maybe not a <i>good</i> guy, but perhaps a <i>better</i> guy.<br>It made me look at the character differently, at any rate.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1509035049ra/24286088.gif" width="400" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>Princeps' Fury</b> was an improvement on the last installment for me in a lot of ways, but there was still a bit too much <i>wah, wah, wah</i> boring shit about battle strategy and other descriptive questing nonsense. I tend to skim that sort of thing to get to (what I consider) the good stuff. However, at least this time around there was a lot more action to hold my attention.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1509035049ra/24286089.gif" width="400" height="250" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>If you loved the other books, you'll love this one.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4254329554960688839" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1409271254?book_show_action=true">Oct 05, 2015</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">

              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5876927101488988955">Do not even try to read the blurb for this book as its first sentence gives a spoiler of the size of a blue whale (I mean the bigger specimens of that sea mammal):<br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1445011303i/16586966._SX540_.jpg' width='340' height='260' alt='Blue whale size' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/>Fortunately here I am, describing the plot while trying to minimize the spoilers. <br/><br/>The other title for the book which works even better would be Tavi Come Home.<br/>Yes, I am thinking about this movie: <br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1445011584i/16586987._SX540_.jpg' width='340' height='260' alt='Lassie Come Home' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/>The big bad enemy of Alera is back and it got bigger and badder this time. <br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1445011708i/16586991.png' width='340' height='260' alt='Big Bad Wolf' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/>Believe it or not, the image is highly appropriate. <br/><br/>Usually Tavi s</span>
  <span id="freeText5876927101488988955" style="display:none">Do not even try to read the blurb for this book as its first sentence gives a spoiler of the size of a blue whale (I mean the bigger specimens of that sea mammal):<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1445011303i/16586966._SX540_.jpg" width="340" height="260" alt="Blue whale size" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>Fortunately here I am, describing the plot while trying to minimize the spoilers. <br><br>The other title for the book which works even better would be Tavi Come Home.<br>Yes, I am thinking about this movie: <br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1445011584i/16586987._SX540_.jpg" width="340" height="260" alt="Lassie Come Home" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>The big bad enemy of Alera is back and it got bigger and badder this time. <br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1445011708i/16586991.png" width="340" height="260" alt="Big Bad Wolf" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>Believe it or not, the image is highly appropriate. <br><br>Usually Tavi saves the day, but this time he is away in a foreign land which - the land that is - is in even worse shape than Alera. So while Tavi and the people he travels with try to survive, Alerans try to do the same but none believes they can actually do it. <br><br>Well, that was obscure and very generic, just like the meaning of the following (this was one of the first results for Google Image search of "Obscure"):<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1445011942i/16587003.jpg" width="340" height="260" alt="Obscure" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>There are practically no spoilers in here though. How does one describe the plot of fifth book of a series which tells one big story? <br><br>The development of characters while not drastic or big still continues in this installment. Tavi does show weaknesses and some faults and does not look like this anymore: <br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1445012917i/16587063.gif" width="340" height="260" alt="Flat" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>The novel is similar to previous four: desperate epic battles, last-minute escapes, heroics, backstabbing politics, exotic enemies and even more exotic allies, <s>Pokémon</s> I mean Furies - these are all here. <br><br>Five books down, one more to go. I jumped straight to the last book right after finishing this one. This was an easy decision considering that while previous four novels each had some conclusion, this one does not exactly end in a cliffhanger, but it has no satisfying resolution whatsoever. <br><br>P.S. If a cover shows an event that happens one page before the epilogue, can it be considered a spoiler?<br></span>

<div id="review_134605031" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/134605031" />
    <a title="Stephen" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1413439-stephen"><img alt="Stephen" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1311616811p2/1413439.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/134605031?book_show_action=true">Dec 11, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Stephen" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Stephen" href="/user/show/1413439-stephen">Stephen</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1413439-stephen?shelf=audiobook">audiobook</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1413439-stephen?shelf=tolkienesque">tolkienesque</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1413439-stephen?shelf=ebooks">ebooks</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1413439-stephen?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1413439-stephen?shelf=2006-2010">2006-2010</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1413439-stephen?shelf=political-fiction">political-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer134605031" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13844654897590746001"><b>Sadly</b>, this is a classic example of a <b>star crossed</b> reader/book relationship. <a href='http://s153.photobucket.com/albums/s207/sullypython/Goodreads/?action=view&current=tumblr_lsqndlc16H1qmf9gqo1_500-1.jpg' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380342424i/698158.jpg' alt='Photobucket' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><br/>I am only giving this <b>3.0 stars</b> and yet I have almost nothing but <b>positive</b> comments to make about the novel. This is a well-written, terrific story with a nice <b>balance</b> between <b>detail</b> and <b>pacing</b> and with characters drawn and developed with enough <b>weight</b> that you can really care about them. The problem is simply that <b>traditional</b> high, epic fantasy and I have lately just not been <b>clicking</b>. It's all become a big, confus</span>
  <span id="freeText13844654897590746001" style="display:none"><b>Sadly</b>, this is a classic example of a <b>star crossed</b> reader/book relationship. <a href="http://s153.photobucket.com/albums/s207/sullypython/Goodreads/?action=view&amp;current=tumblr_lsqndlc16H1qmf9gqo1_500-1.jpg" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380342424i/698158.jpg" alt="Photobucket" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>I am only giving this <b>3.0 stars</b> and yet I have almost nothing but <b>positive</b> comments to make about the novel. This is a well-written, terrific story with a nice <b>balance</b> between <b>detail</b> and <b>pacing</b> and with characters drawn and developed with enough <b>weight</b> that you can really care about them. The problem is simply that <b>traditional</b> high, epic fantasy and I have lately just not been <b>clicking</b>. It's all become a big, confusing mess of best intentions and shattered expectations and I'm mostly to blame. <br><br>Therefore, to this book and all other well done high fantasy epics*, let me say: <b>it’s not you, it’s me</b>. <br><br><i>*The above statement does <b>not</b> apply to the over abundance of crappy, “paint by numbers” never-ending <b>BLOAT-athons</b> that seem to <b>meander</b> and <b>ramble</b> on for decades without inching any closer to the finish line. In your case, it is definitely you that is the problem and your capacity for suckage has never been greater.</i> <br><a href="http://s153.photobucket.com/albums/s207/sullypython/Fail/?action=view&amp;current=facepalm-baby-2.jpg" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380342424i/698159.jpg" alt="Photobucket" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>Based on the above and my comments below, when evaluating my rating to determine whether this book is right for you, please adjust upwards as follows:<br><br>1. If, excluding Lord of the Rings, more than half of your 10 favorite books are within the traditional, epic fantasy genre, <b>add one star</b> to my rating. <br><br>2. If the vast majority of your favorite books are traditional tolkienesque fantasy and you are also a fan of Butcher’s “Dresden Series,” <b>add 2 stars</b> as this is a no-brainer 5 star read for you. <br><br>3. If you have slept outside of a book store waiting to be the first in line to have Terry Brooks and/or Terry Goodkind sign either a copy of their newest book or a part of your body… than <b>[******censored******]</b> and I don’t know what else to say to you. <br><br><b><u>PLOT SUMMARY</u>:</b><br><br><i><u>Potential spoiler warning</u>:</i> While I won’t divulge any of the critical events of this book, my plot summary will include reference to doings and goings on from the first four installments. <br>.<br>.<br>.<br>.<br>.<br>So book 5 picks up shortly after the end of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/346087.Captain_s_Fury__Codex_Alera___4_" title="Captain's Fury (Codex Alera, #4) by Jim Butcher" rel="nofollow noopener">Captain's Fury</a>, in which Tavi was revealed to be the heir to the crown of Alera (i.e., the main human civilization patterned on ancient Rome). He has thus been elevated to the rank of Princeps and become among the most powerful individual in the country. Given the significant amount of political intrigue woven into the fabric of this series, you can imagine the plotting, scheming and other <s>sordid</s> assorted Machiavellian machinations brought to bear by factions trying to monkey-wrench Tavi’s elevation and new status.<br> <br>Meanwhile, it turns out that the parasitic, <b>body-snatching-body-cloning</b> Vord have been much busier bees than anyone anticipated and the <b>threat level</b> has gone from very serious to “holy shit we’re all going to die.” Even the combined might of the fury-crafting Alerans and their new allies, the wolf-like Canim, do not appear adequate to save the planet from becoming <b>Vord-kabobs</b>. Their only hope appears to be <s>Obi-Wan Kenobi</s> to add to the alliance the strength of the mysterious Icemen who have been engaged in a bitter war with the Alerans for millennia out beyond the giant northern wall.**<br><br>**I know what you are thinking and, YES, the giant northern wall bears a striking resemblance to <b>The Wall</b> in George R.R. Martin’s Song of Ice and Fire and I think Jimmy Butcher owes Martin a fruit basket as a thank you. <br><br><b><u>THOUGHTS</u>:</b><br><br>This is skillfully crafted, rock solid traditional epic fantasy that I can completely understand fans of the genre <b>slobbering</b> all over. If this is your bag <s>baby</s>, than I certainly recommend this series as it is vastly superior in both writing and story to much of the aimless, <b>ham-fisted drek</b> that passes for large scale fantasy. Butcher has a gift for creating interesting magic systems and his elemental-based furies (fire, water, earth and air) is well defined and nicely done. His world-building is thoughtful and deftly spliced into the narrative and the characters are given room to breathe and differentiate themselves from one another. <br><br>Put simply, It’s good quality. <br><br>That said, for me personally this is just a bit too “traditional” and I’ve become seriously burned out on this kind of setting. While I still enjoy the truly grim side of epic fantasy as exemplified by the aforementioned <i>Song of Ice and Fire</i> by George Martin, most of my favorite recent fantasies have been either of the hip, swashbuckling variety (e.g., Steven Brust’s <i>“Jhereg”</i> series and Scott Lynch’s <i>“Gentlemen Bastards”</i> series) or of the truly <b>subversive</b> strain such as Joe Abercrombie’s <i>“First Law”</i> trilogy and Richard Morgan’s <i>“Land Fit for Heroes.”</i><br><br>Thus, I was just never fully engaged in the story and it made for long, somewhat tiresome read during which I was constantly prone to distraction. I would be staring off into the middle distance and then something interesting would jerk my attention back to the story...only to have my attention wander off again a few minutes later. <br><br>And so on and so on….rinse and repeat. <br><br>In sum, an excellent traditional epic fantasy that I completely failed as a reader. This book and this series deserve someone better…maybe someone like you. <br><br>3.0 stars. <br></span>
  <a data-text-id="13844654897590746001" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2945331906" />
    <a title="Nadine" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3759963-nadine"><img alt="Nadine" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1566849081p2/3759963.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2945331906?book_show_action=true">Oct 01, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nadine" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nadine" href="/user/show/3759963-nadine">Nadine</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Mass Market Paperback 9780441017966" href="/book/show/6303648-princeps-fury">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2945331906" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3681799577068462944">My reviews for these novels keep getting shorter and shorter. I dislike writing reviews for sequels since I find it hard to write about the novel without spoiling anything.<br/><br/>I have been skimming reviews for Princeps’ Fury and found that many people rated this as their least favourite of the series. I, however, thoroughly enjoyed Princeps’ Fury and its set up for the final novel, First Lord’s Fury. I especially enjoyed the final few pages.<br/><br/>Isana’s chapters are usually not my favourite since they are</span>
  <span id="freeText3681799577068462944" style="display:none">My reviews for these novels keep getting shorter and shorter. I dislike writing reviews for sequels since I find it hard to write about the novel without spoiling anything.<br /><br />I have been skimming reviews for Princeps’ Fury and found that many people rated this as their least favourite of the series. I, however, thoroughly enjoyed Princeps’ Fury and its set up for the final novel, First Lord’s Fury. I especially enjoyed the final few pages.<br /><br />Isana’s chapters are usually not my favourite since they are not as action packed or detail oriented as Tavi’s or Amara’s, however Isana’s chapters in Princeps’ Fury are incredible. Not only do readers get to see Isana in a new badass light, but also readers are treated to some interesting world building that had me rereading certain passages.<br /><br />Tavi’s campaign and exploration of the Cane homeland were some of the best parts of the novel. I am always a fan of new or game changing information no matter how far in the series it comes.<br /><br />That is about all I can say without spoiling anything more than the title already spoils. I am very excited to read the final novel, though I may procrastinate a bit since I do not want this story to end.<br /><br />As always, I highly recommend this series. It’s fun and easy to read with badass characters and an interesting magic system.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="3681799577068462944" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1437103321" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

    <a title="Kathleen" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/13954899-kathleen"><img alt="Kathleen" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1365166675p2/13954899.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1437103321?book_show_action=true">Nov 08, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kathleen" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kathleen" href="/user/show/13954899-kathleen">Kathleen</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13954899-kathleen?shelf=audio">audio</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13954899-kathleen?shelf=magic-fantasy">magic-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13954899-kathleen?shelf=series">series</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1437103321" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16998921631657373662">In a fantastical setting, this plot involves a desperate and clever escape from hoards of merciless invaders. I enjoyed it, even though the plot didn't seem to require a whole book. But Butcher certainly created a sense of emergency. Apocalypse. Some sweet scenes (breakfast on the ship), some poignant scenes (reunion) and some surprising scenes (no telling).<br/><br/>I like the Canum wolf-people, including Varg and his son Nasaug. We also meet the Icemen, but...huh...they didn't add much to the book. Mayb</span>
  <span id="freeText16998921631657373662" style="display:none">In a fantastical setting, this plot involves a desperate and clever escape from hoards of merciless invaders. I enjoyed it, even though the plot didn't seem to require a whole book. But Butcher certainly created a sense of emergency. Apocalypse. Some sweet scenes (breakfast on the ship), some poignant scenes (reunion) and some surprising scenes (no telling).<br /><br />I like the Canum wolf-people, including Varg and his son Nasaug. We also meet the Icemen, but...huh...they didn't add much to the book. Maybe they'll play a larger role in the next book. The Vord are the big bad once again, with some nasty surprises there, and some predicted tropes. A sad death takes place, but we also spend lots of time with a handful of characters we've learned to love across the series: Tavi, Katai, Crassus. Max. Ehren, etc etc etc<br /><br />Butcher writes well. But I'm tired of "wolfish grin" (repetitive description for how men smile). Also, his portrayal of Isana's character is inconsistent. <br /><br />I am not sure I like where Butcher is going with a certain traitor. He's a ruthless, murderous character who in past novels showed himself to be a pathetically poor judge of character. Redemption should not be so easy.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="16998921631657373662" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer38676962&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer38676962" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7535092168581562948">Another superb book in the codex alera. The novel has three or four plot lines going on at once. Tavi is in the Canim homeland where he finds the Vord swarming. At home in Alera, the Vord have attacked and although Gaius has a plan he is weak and ill. He dispatches Tavi's mother north to get the Legions led by Maximus and Crassus father, but first she has to make peace with the Icemen. Gaius also dispatches Amara and Bernard on a secret mission to find out how the Vord are fury crafting and stop</span>
  <span id="freeText7535092168581562948" style="display:none">Another superb book in the codex alera. The novel has three or four plot lines going on at once. Tavi is in the Canim homeland where he finds the Vord swarming. At home in Alera, the Vord have attacked and although Gaius has a plan he is weak and ill. He dispatches Tavi's mother north to get the Legions led by Maximus and Crassus father, but first she has to make peace with the Icemen. Gaius also dispatches Amara and Bernard on a secret mission to find out how the Vord are fury crafting and stop it. All of the stories move quickly to a conclusion, but Tavi's ingenuity is again the real star of this novel.<br /><br />This book is the fifth in a continuous series and readers would be ill served to start here<br /><br />As expected this is not the last of the codex alera, and I for one am glad b/c the story is still fresh and fun.<br /><br /></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer6581984730542115055">Again, no bloody map in the book! The only maps are in the 3d & 6th books. I paid over $10 each for these paperbacks, so you'd think they could spring for a damn map. There's a good selection here:<br/><a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='http://www.jim-butcher.com/posts/2009/codex-alera-map'>http://www.jim-butcher.com/posts/2009...</a><br/>They're supposed to be for your computer wall paper, but print out in monochrome well.<br/><br/><a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='http://www.jimbutcheronline.com/bb/index.php/topic,5303.0.html'>http://www.jimbutcheronline.com/bb/in...</a><br/>contains a lot of maps of specific areas. I didn't find it all that useful & there are maps throughout the series, so it contains spoiler</span>
  <span id="freeText6581984730542115055" style="display:none">Again, no bloody map in the book! The only maps are in the 3d &amp; 6th books. I paid over $10 each for these paperbacks, so you'd think they could spring for a damn map. There's a good selection here:<br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.jim-butcher.com/posts/2009/codex-alera-map">http://www.jim-butcher.com/posts/2009...</a><br />They're supposed to be for your computer wall paper, but print out in monochrome well.<br /><br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.jimbutcheronline.com/bb/index.php/topic,5303.0.html">http://www.jimbutcheronline.com/bb/in...</a><br />contains a lot of maps of specific areas. I didn't find it all that useful &amp; there are maps throughout the series, so it contains spoilers.<br /><br />Again, this was a fun romp without any real surprises or emotional hits. Butcher could have easily made it a tougher, more emotional ride, but instead he takes the easy way out most of the time. I enjoyed the Belgariad too, though. In many ways this series reminds me of that. Not bad, but certainly not great literature.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6581984730542115055" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1687176390" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1687176390" />
    <a title="Jenna Kathleen" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/32846944-jenna-kathleen"><img alt="Jenna Kathleen" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1583785298p2/32846944.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1687176390?book_show_action=true">Jan 31, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jenna Kathleen" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jenna Kathleen" href="/user/show/32846944-jenna-kathleen">Jenna Kathleen</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32846944-jenna-kathleen?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1687176390" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18101395158249413035">There have been ups and downs throughout this series. There were moments when I was emotionally hurting because of what has happened to the characters, moments I suddenly perked up and my eyes enlarged in anticipation, moments when I felt complete satisfaction for a story coming to a close and moments I was thankful I had the next book because the one I had just read ended on such a perfect cliffhanger. This book had almost none of these moments.<br/><br/>After 5 books, I am pretty attached to some of the</span>
  <span id="freeText18101395158249413035" style="display:none">There have been ups and downs throughout this series. There were moments when I was emotionally hurting because of what has happened to the characters, moments I suddenly perked up and my eyes enlarged in anticipation, moments when I felt complete satisfaction for a story coming to a close and moments I was thankful I had the next book because the one I had just read ended on such a perfect cliffhanger. This book had almost none of these moments.<br /><br />After 5 books, I am pretty attached to some of these characters. Most of them have had really good character development throughout the series so the one thing I liked about this book was that I was still with them. Unfortunately, I really had to slog through most of this one to have that positive experience. Tavi's character didn't really grow, but we heard all about how clever he is over and over again. I like Tavi, but I already know that he's clever. Let's see that brilliant mind at work rather than just hear about it.<br /><br />I'm all for good eucatastrophy. It's what makes fantasy believable: epic events that show how awesome our favourite characters are, offset by tragedy. Even fantastic worlds aren't perfect. But Alera freaking sucks. I like villains that take wit and awesome powers to defeat, but <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[the only defeat in this book was on the side of the Alerans <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>.<br /><br />The awesome epic successes of the main characters were a lot less awesome and epic that the previous books in this series and I was just never really satisfied with anything great that happened to the characters because it happened after a monumental wave of failure and slog. At that point, I didn't even feel bad for them, but rather, I started questioning the author. <br /><br />When things starting coming together, a lot of the things felt unbelievable. For example: <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[All of the sudden Tavi had enough furycrafters to make and maintain ships so giant they couldn't even fit in the port? Yet they couldn't defeat the uncoordinated Vord lacking enough queens to keep them organized...? <br />Also, the slave collar on Amara, I didn't see coming, but it also wasn't really believable. All of the sudden pleasure and desire washed over her when Brentis put the collar on, but she already had a collar on. Why wasn't she feeling that way before?  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br />These are just two things, but these two made me question the veracity of the events of the book and the powers of the characters.<br /><br />Here's to hoping that this one was just setting up for a phenomenal ending in book 6.</span>
  <a data-text-id="18101395158249413035" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_46515694" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/46515694" />
    <a title="Kate Coombs" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/235385-kate-coombs"><img alt="Kate Coombs" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1231619578p2/235385.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/46515694?book_show_action=true">Feb 16, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kate Coombs" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kate Coombs" href="/user/show/235385-kate-coombs">Kate Coombs</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer46515694" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6903533146904153908">My five stars are for the entire series, but I'm too busy (lazy!) to write a review for each book. I had faithfully read all of the Dresden Files books, but was less interested in the Alera series. Then I picked up the first one, and pretty soon I was madly reading the other four, completely engrossed. When I read something this compelling, I'm reminded why I'm a Reader!<br/><br/>When we first meet our hero, Tavi, he lives on a steadholt in the outer reaches of Alera with his uncle Bernard and his aunt Is</span>
  <span id="freeText6903533146904153908" style="display:none">My five stars are for the entire series, but I'm too busy (lazy!) to write a review for each book. I had faithfully read all of the Dresden Files books, but was less interested in the Alera series. Then I picked up the first one, and pretty soon I was madly reading the other four, completely engrossed. When I read something this compelling, I'm reminded why I'm a Reader!<br /><br />When we first meet our hero, Tavi, he lives on a steadholt in the outer reaches of Alera with his uncle Bernard and his aunt Isana (brother and sister, not a married couple). Bernard has a magical gift for earthcrafting, while Isana has a gift for watercrafting--gifts called furies that partly shape the social hierarchy in Alera. To his great dismay, Tavi is furyless. This makes him something like a cripple in his society.<br /><br />The Alera books are about political scheming, lost heirs, and deadly enemies. They also spend a lot of time on military campaigns. Tavi overcomes his lack of gifts through wiliness, good sense, and diplomacy--he's one for creative problem solving. But when the ruthless Vord invade Alera (kind of like Star Trek's Borg, only more organic and with creepy new aspects), even Tavi's cleverness may not be enough.<br /><br />I lost myself in these stories and found myself rooting for these characters. Highly recommended for sci-fi/fantasy readers!</span>
  <a data-text-id="6903533146904153908" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText17210214067840143545" style="display:none">By this fifth volume all I'm interested in is to finish this series and get it over with.<br />It's not that it's a badly written story, or that the characters are unlikable, it's just that the plot is so ridiculously apocalyptic, the dialogue bombastically heroic and the good guys always face ridiculous odds and almost always come up to fight another day. The one exception is easy to guess if you check the title of the next book.<br />This fifth volume maintains the tone and the pace set in the previous books, only raising the stacks higher and higher. Few new characters are introduced (we get to see the Icewall and a part of a new continent), so the story is very easy to follow and Butcher style makes little demands from the reader.<br />Another reader made a spot on observation in a forum that some of the new fantasy authors make the mistake of going into a new series with all guns blazing and equip their heroes with superpowers. And later on in the epic they are stuck, having to come up with bigger and bigger threats, stronger than strong magic and impossible odds to overcome. I think this is what happened with Codex Alera.<br />Fortunately, there is only one more book to put my compulsion to finish series I've started to rest.</span>

<div id="review_103420415" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/103420415" />
    <a title="M.F. Soriano" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3415061-m-f-soriano"><img alt="M.F. Soriano" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442894603p2/3415061.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/103420415?book_show_action=true">May 19, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="M.F. Soriano" class="user" itemprop="url" name="M.F. Soriano" href="/user/show/3415061-m-f-soriano">M.F. Soriano</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer103420415" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13504856953674898942">An epic fantasy series that's getting too epic for it's own good. A lot of the fun in the first novels came from big personalities colliding, and from the sense of skill and resourcefulness shown by the protagonists during those collisions. The best parts in this book follow similar parameters, but the series' need to continue raising the stakes has forced most of the rest of the plot into bloated battles featuring hundreds of thousands of combatants. There isn't much room, anymore, for the clev</span>
  <span id="freeText13504856953674898942" style="display:none">An epic fantasy series that's getting too epic for it's own good. A lot of the fun in the first novels came from big personalities colliding, and from the sense of skill and resourcefulness shown by the protagonists during those collisions. The best parts in this book follow similar parameters, but the series' need to continue raising the stakes has forced most of the rest of the plot into bloated battles featuring hundreds of thousands of combatants. There isn't much room, anymore, for the clever details and the personal drama that made the first books exciting--now it's just blurry masses of bodies moving. I also feel like the author, who's shown remarkable creativity up to this point, is finally reaching the limits of his imagination. This book, like the others, did have a few moments where I found myself thinking "What a great idea!" But I didn't feel quite the same level of delight when I had those thoughts this time. I'm not sure if the ideas just aren't as good as they were, or if, at this point, there have been so many great ideas that the magic has finally started to feel mundane.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13504856953674898942" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_534338733" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/534338733" />
    <a title="Richard" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1662632-richard"><img alt="Richard" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1540855273p2/1662632.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/534338733?book_show_action=true">Feb 12, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Richard" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Richard" href="/user/show/1662632-richard">Richard</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Fans of epic fantasy and/or the Dresden Files</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1662632-richard?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1662632-richard?shelf=fantasy-magic">fantasy-magic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1662632-richard?shelf=series">series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1662632-richard?shelf=fantasy-epic">fantasy-epic</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer534338733" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17436474470708669429">I finished all six volumes in Jim Butcher’s <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/series/45545' rel='nofollow noopener'>Codex Alera</a> series, so I’m writing one review to cover the whole set. Regardless of which of the books this review is attached to, if you want to read this epic saga, start with the first book: <i>
  <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/29396.Furies_of_Calderon__Codex_Alera___1_' title='Furies of Calderon (Codex Alera, #1) by Jim Butcher' rel='nofollow noopener'>Furies of Calderon</a>
</i>. I’ve also read all <i>fourteen</i> of the full-length books in his <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/series/40346' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <i>Dresden Files</i>
</a>, and there are some interesting points of comparison.<br/><br/>First and foremost, this is a well-crafted and engrossing tale — definitely worth reading.<br/><br/>The tale follows </span>
  <span id="freeText17436474470708669429" style="display:none">I finished all six volumes in Jim Butcher’s <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/series/45545" rel="nofollow noopener">Codex Alera</a> series, so I’m writing one review to cover the whole set. Regardless of which of the books this review is attached to, if you want to read this epic saga, start with the first book: <i>
  <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/29396.Furies_of_Calderon__Codex_Alera___1_" title="Furies of Calderon (Codex Alera, #1) by Jim Butcher" rel="nofollow noopener">Furies of Calderon</a>
</i>. I’ve also read all <i>fourteen</i> of the full-length books in his <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/series/40346" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <i>Dresden Files</i>
</a>, and there are some interesting points of comparison.<br><br>First and foremost, this is a well-crafted and engrossing tale — definitely worth reading.<br><br>The tale follows the life of young Tavi of the backwater province of Calderon over the course of several years, as his world is riven by existential threats and as he grows up and plays a larger and larger role. There really isn’t anything fundamentally innovative here — most of the elements of the plot are echoed in other epic fantasies. The system of magic plays a large role and is well thought-out, but while it is fresh, it isn’t radical. What makes <i>Codex Alera</i> an excellent addition to the fantasy shelf is in the story and its telling. The characters are engaging and adequately complex, the plot starts well and grows satisfyingly convoluted, and there is plenty of action to drive things forward.<br><br>Because the story begins when Tavi is still only fifteen, the first volume is weaker than the sequels. His relationships and option for acting aren’t as complex as they soon become, and his circle of acquaintances is also more limited. Starting with the second book, the scope of story broadens dramatically, with a wider range of characters getting in-depth treatment. Eventually, Butcher brings a small measure of romance into the mix, with even a little non-puritanical treatment of sex. Considering how poorly these last topics are dealt with in the <i>Dresden Files</i>, that’s a nice change.<br><br>Fans of the <i>Dresden Files</i> will still find some aspects of the tone and style very familiar. Since the new series is set in a completely fictional world (as opposed to contemporary Chicago), the ironic sarcasm is toned down dramatically, but there is still plenty around. All the clever characters still banter and tease, especially in times of mortal peril. This isn’t exactly a rare device in genre fiction (and probably anachronistic here, given the period is a rough approximation of feudalism, to the extent that can apply to fantasy), but Butcher does it pretty well.<br><br><i>Codex Alera</i> is a more mature effort, though. The earlier series is locked into a first-person narrative, for example, which means the voice of a single character is loud, flaws and all. Here, instead, there are several point-of-view characters, although unfortunately Butcher only lets us hear the thoughts of his protagonists. As limiting as that still is, there is more psychological depth. A major theme that grows more pressing through the series is the inevitable compromises a leader must make between opposing values, and how horrifying it is to be required to make decisions whose outcomes are all nauseating. Because the various viewpoint characters are at differing points in their understanding of this <a href="https://plato.stanford.edu/entries/dirty-hands/" rel="nofollow noopener">“dirty hands”</a> dynamic, Butcher can simultaneously illuminate a ruler’s imperative for pragmatism as well as the revulsion towards apparent amorality felt by those not confronted with the need for decisive action.<br><br>Unfortunately, there is also still a bit too much untimely introspection and moralising. The multiple viewpoints ameliorate this a bit, but we’re still treated to characters pausing in the middle of a tense situation (a battle scene, for example, or a political debate) and expounding on their personal convictions — which aren’t particularly interesting, since they are fairly predictable. This is another aspect that makes the first book weaker — because Tavi is still growing emotionally, there are too many opportunities for the author to indulge himself with the self-righteous attitudes of adolescence.<br><br>Butcher has a long way to go before he can honestly portray real nuance in personality types. Judging by both series, I’d bet that he’s what I’ll call a “heartland liberal”. His heroes are socially progressive multiculturalists, without much tolerance for faiths or creeds that require uncritical obedience. Religions are frequently portrayed benevolently, but religious <i>leaders</i> seem to be corrupt even more often than other powerful characters. Butcher portrays political and military institutions in a somewhat more favorable light. While both have plenty of power-hungry and venal characters, he depicts kings and generals as responsible people struggling to do the right thing.<br><br>Where the nuance is missing is in a genuinely sympathetic portrayal of those that don’t fit his morality. For example, late in the series there is a conflict between the secular leaders of a military group and its religious leadership. The flaws of the latter group are quite plausible, but make things morally simplistic. Instead of having two groups both of which are honestly striving to do the right thing, one of the two has already made choices that signify their corruption. Even though Butcher doesn’t fall into the common trap of casting the whole story into a good-versus-evil conflict (<i>a la</i> Sauron of Mordor, or the Dark Side of the Force, or the Death Eaters, <i>et cetera ad nauseum</i>), he still relies on evil at the individual level. The good might be complex, but his villains really aren’t.<br><br>Granted, that’s asking a lot. The much more experienced George R. R. Martin has humanized a few of his villains in his <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/series/43790" rel="nofollow noopener">Song of Ice and Fire series</a>, but he generally still makes it hard to like them. Martin’s real strength is that he makes it harder to actually decide who is a villain. Butcher’s stories are still morally unambiguous, even with his gradually growing skill at giving us characters that struggle with their choices in increasingly realistic ways.<br><br>Oh, by the way: this might help. There was, frustratingly, no map in the editions I read until the final volume. But Butcher’s website provides this one (click through to a larger version):<blockquote>
  <a href="http://www.jim-butcher.com/pics/map1280x1024.jpg" rel="nofollow noopener">
    <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1379739956i/67478._SX540_.jpg" width="500" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
  </a>
</blockquote><i>The first book in the series was the fantasy selection for the Goodreads <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/group/show/1865.SciFi_and_Fantasy_Book_Club" rel="nofollow noopener">SciFi and Fantasy Book Club</a> for the month of July 2010. Visit <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/group/show_book/1865.SciFi_and_Fantasy_Book_Club?group_book_id=262274" rel="nofollow noopener">this link</a> to see all of the discussions, group member reviews, etc.</i><br>­</span>
  <a data-text-id="17436474470708669429" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2106251344" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2106251344" />
    <a title="Kostas" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/25638423-kostas"><img alt="Kostas" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1554812738p2/25638423.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2106251344?book_show_action=true">May 22, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kostas" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kostas" href="/user/show/25638423-kostas">Kostas</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Mass Market Paperback 9780441017966" href="/book/show/6303648-princeps-fury">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25638423-kostas?shelf=epic-high-fantasy">epic-high-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25638423-kostas?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25638423-kostas?shelf=military-sff">military-sff</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2106251344" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4233690529113725087">8.5/10<br/><br/>With the series approaching closer and closer to its end, and the much-anticipated culmination of the story and the characters, Jim Butcher brings us in the <i>Princeps' Fury</i>, the fifth installment, into the greatest threat that has ever appeared in the Realm of Alera, into a story of seafarers and Warmasters, diplomats, primitive northerners, and chitinous monsters, and into an adventure of subjugation and annihilation, acceptance and compromise, and faith and fealty, that will judge the fat</span>
  <span id="freeText4233690529113725087" style="display:none">8.5/10<br /><br />With the series approaching closer and closer to its end, and the much-anticipated culmination of the story and the characters, Jim Butcher brings us in the <i>Princeps' Fury</i>, the fifth installment, into the greatest threat that has ever appeared in the Realm of Alera, into a story of seafarers and Warmasters, diplomats, primitive northerners, and chitinous monsters, and into an adventure of subjugation and annihilation, acceptance and compromise, and faith and fealty, that will judge the fate of the world.<br /><br />Some months have passed since the war in the western reaches of the Realm, and the difficulties they had to face; an illogical campaign that put to the test their very beliefs, causing a conflict that left in its wale only more suffering and misery, and now, with the coastal cities to have suffered the greatest disasters, the refugees of Alera have begun again to try and search in their lives what they lost - but for Tavi, with his heritage having been revealed across the world, making him for some a hope and for others a threat, these months were nothing but full of swift preparations.<br />Sailing away from the harbor of the town of Mastings, the base of their mutual operations, in an expedition to reach a foreign land through the deep blue sea, Tavi has been traveling the better part of their two-month voyage aboard Captain Demos’s <i>Slive</i>, guiding along with the Legions of the First Aleran and Free Aleran the ships of the Canim and their forces back to their homeland, to Canea, where no Aleran has yet stepped onto before.<br />Yet, with their voyage in the open sea to have taken them through dangerous waters, as he’ll try to open a communication with the rest of the Canim castes - wishing to learn as quickly as possible the fate of the land - when an indescribable horror that has haunted his dreams comes true, and Warmaster Lararl, in his zeal to prove himself worthy before his kin, sets to protect his self-interests, Tavi and his comrades will soon find themselves trapped and surrounded by deadly enemies, facing a dilemma that may well judge the salvation of a foreign people from its certain extinction.<br /><br />Back in Alera, at the fortress of Garrison, Amara, having experienced the pain of betrayal once again by someone who she thought she admired and respected most, has spent these months among the folk of Calderon Valley and in Bernard’s company, trying to heal the wounds in her soul that so burn her, and making the final preparations for their formal union that might finally bring them a little happiness.<br />But, as the arrival of a sudden message demands of them their immediate attendance in the Capital, when the First Lord presents himself before the villagers, the Citizens, the Senators and the High Lords, shaking their lives with a revelation as never before, Amara and Bernard will have to take on a dangerous mission that will lead them at the heart of a deadly enemy; a mission that, if they do not leave back their enmities of the past behind, and find again the courage to do the impossible, it could very easily prove and their last.<br />At the same time, Isana, having sought refuge in High Lady Placida’s household after the last events, when she gets assigned to travel in a diplomatic mission to the northern borders, beyond the city of Antillus and the Shieldwall where men and children alike have sacrificed their lives against the primitive Icemen over the centuries, she’ll find herself into her own challenges that will make the Realm’s desperate need for peace from that front even more difficult to its achievement; while Ehren, having escaped from the forces of the chitinous monsters with a terrible secret, he’ll try to help the First Lord to prepare the Legions against a nightmarish horde that they have only minimum chances to survive.<br /><br />However, with the Realm of Alera coming for the first time after a thousand years against its greatest threat, when the Vord queen sends its forces against the defending Legions of the Capital, and far away in the Canim homeland the uncontrollable chitinous monsters surge toward the last standing survivors, Tavi and his comrades, Amara and Bernard, Isana and Aria, and Ehren and the First Lord, will have to leave their differences aside and fight this new threat before all is lost, because if they fail to overcome these difficulties, their very survival will hang in the balance.<br /><br />Entering the final stages of the characters’ adventures, having built since the beginning an epic journey full of wonders and magic, Jim Butcher - lead by the events of the previous book, the <i>Captain’s Fury</i> - takes us for the first time in the entire series to Canea, the homeland of the Canim, bring before us their great cities that, divided amongst the strongest leaders, have become the center of their power, their different societies, consisting from makers and artisans to warriors and ritualists, and the codes they follow; as well as to the Realm’s northern borders, beyond the Shieldwall and their defending cities, giving us a glimpse of the primitive race of the Icemen, the reasons for their hostilities, and the rules and beliefs with which they live by.<br />But bringing us at the same time and closer than ever before into the Vord hives, and their powerful queens who rule through the <i>croach</i> - the gelatinous green substance that can devour anything living - giving them the ability to produce nightmarish creatures at rapid paces, creating warriors of vastly superior strength and ability - three races that, in contrast to the seemingly ideals of the people of Alera, shows along with the Marat barbarians their immense differences but also the grandeur of this world.<br /><br />And, bringing this epic journey a step closer toward its completion, Butcher immerses us in the <i>Princeps’ Fury</i> into the greatest threat that has come to the Realm of Alera for more than a thousand years, mixing once again politics with war, and duels with self-interests, traveling us through the western seas, the north and the south into a story of diplomats, Warmasters, High Lords, primitive savages, chitinous monsters and nightmarish queens, and into an adventure of subjugation, annihilation, compromise, survival, and faith and fealty, that creates in the end a surge of emotions, raising the expectations for the final book even further.<br /><br />In conclusion, the <i>Princeps’ Fury</i> is one of the stronger books in the series, with Jim Butcher - bringing the characters’ adventures one step closer toward their completion - to takes us into a new, great war, traveling us into a story of seafarers, Warmasters, primitive northerners, and chitinous monsters, but also into an adventure of annihilation, compromise and fealty that leaves however many issues open to be solve in the sixth and final book.<br /><br /><br />Ελληνική κριτική:<br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Με την σειρά να πλησιάζει όλο και πιο κοντά στο τέλος της, και την πολυαναμενόμενη αποκορύφωση της ιστορίας και των χαρακτήρων, ο Jim Butcher μας φέρνει στο <i>Princeps’ Fury</i>, το πέμπτο μέρος, μέσα στην μεγαλύτερη απειλή που έχει εμφανιστεί ποτέ στο Βασίλειο της Alera, μέσα σε μια ιστορία θαλασσοπόρων και Πολεμάρχων, διπλωματών, πρωτόγονων κατοίκων του βορρά, και χιτινωδών τεράτων, και σε μια περιπέτεια υποδούλωσης και εκμηδένισης, αποδοχής και συμβιβασμού, και πίστης και αφοσίωσης, που θα κρίνει την μοίρα του κόσμου.<br /><br />Μερικοί μήνες έχουν περάσει από τον πόλεμο στις δυτικές εκτάσεις του Βασιλείου, και τις δυσκολίες που έπρεπε να αντιμετωπίσουν• μια παράλογη εκστρατεία που έβαλε σε δοκιμή τα ίδια τους τα πιστεύω, προκαλώντας μια σύγκρουση που άφησε στο κατόπι της μονάχα περισσότερα βάσανα και δυστυχία, και τώρα, με τις παραλιακές πόλεις να έχουν δεχθεί τις μεγαλύτερες καταστροφές, οι πρόσφυγες της Alera έχουν ξεκινήσει ξανά για να προσπαθήσουν και να αναζητήσουν στις ζωές τους αυτά που έχασαν - αλλά για τον Tavi, με την κληρονομιά του να έχει αποκαλυφθεί σε όλο τον κόσμο, κάνοντάς τον για κάποιους μια ελπίδα και για άλλους μια απειλή, αυτοί οι μήνες δεν ήταν τίποτα περισσότερο παρά γεμάτοι με ταχείες προετοιμασίες.<br />Σαλπάροντας από το λιμάνι της πόλης του Mastings, την βάση των αμοιβαίων τους επιχειρήσεων, σε μια αποστολή για να φτάσουν μια ξένη χώρα μέσα από την βαθιά μπλε θάλασσα, ο Tavi ταξιδεύει το μεγαλύτερο μέρος του δίμηνου ταξιδιού τους επάνω στο Slive του Καπετάνιου Demos, οδηγώντας μαζί τις Λεγεώνες της Πρώτης Αλέριας και της Ελεύθερης Αλέριας τα πλοία των Canim και των δυνάμεών τους πίσω στην πατρίδα τους, την Canea, όπου κανένας Αλέριος έχει ακόμη πατήσει πριν.<br />Κι όμως, με το ταξίδι τους στην ανοιχτή θάλασσα να τους έχει περάσει μέσα από επικίνδυνα νερά, καθώς θα προσπαθήσει να ανοίξει μια επικοινωνία με τις υπόλοιπες κάστες των Canim - επιθυμώντας να μάθει όσο πιο γρήγορα γίνεται την μοίρα της χώρας - όταν μια απερίγραπτη φρίκη που έχει στοιχειώσει τα όνειρά του έρθει αληθινή, και ο Πολέμαρχος Lararl, στον ζήλο του να αποδειχθεί άξιος ενώπιον των συγγενών του, θέσει να προστατέψει τα προσωπικά συμφέροντά του, ο Tavi και οι σύντροφοί του θα βρεθούν σύντομα παγιδευμένοι και περικυκλωμένοι από θανάσιμους εχθρούς, αντιμετωπίζοντας ένα δίλημμα που μπορεί κάλλιστα να κρίνει την σωτηρία ενός ξένου λαού από τον σίγουρο αφανισμό του.<br /><br />Πίσω στην Alera, στο φρούριο του Garrison, η Amara, έχοντας νιώσει για άλλη μια φορά τον πόνο της προδοσίας από κάποιον που νόμιζε ότι θαύμαζε και σεβόταν περισσότερο, έχει περάσει αυτούς του μήνες ανάμεσα στους ανθρώπους της Κοιλάδας του Calderon και στην συντροφιά του Bernard, προσπαθώντας να γιατρέψει της πληγές στην ψυχής της που τόσο την καίνε, και κάνοντας τις τελευταίες προετοιμασίες για την επίσημη ένωσή τους που μπορεί να τους φέρει επιτέλους λίγη ευτυχία.<br />Όμως, καθώς η άφιξη ενός ξαφνικού μηνύματος τους απαιτήσει την άμεση παρουσία τους στην Πρωτεύουσα, όταν ο Πρώτος Άρχοντας παρουσιαστεί ενώπιον των χωριατών, των Πολιτών, των Γερουσιαστών και των Υψηλών Αρχόντων, ταρακουνώντας τις ζωές τους με μια αποκάλυψη όπως ποτέ ξανά, η Amara και ο Bernard θα πρέπει να αναλάβουν μια επικίνδυνη αποστολή που θα τους οδηγήσει στην καρδιά ενός θανάσιμου εχθρού• μια αποστολή που, αν δεν αφήσουν πίσω τις έχθρες του παρελθόντος πίσω, και να βρουν ξανά το κουράγιο για το ακατόρθωτο, θα μπορούσε πολύ εύκολα να αποδειχθεί και η τελευταία τους.<br />Συγχρόνως, η Isana, έχοντας αναζητήσει καταφύγιο στο σπιτικό της Υψηλής Κυρίας Placida μετά τα τελευταία γεγονότα, όταν της ανατεθεί να ταξιδέψει σε μια διπλωματική αποστολή στα βόρεια σύνορα, πέρα από την πόλη της Antillus και το Τοίχος όπου άνδρες και παιδιά ομοίως έχουν θυσιάσει τις ζωές τους ενάντια των πρωτόγονων Ανθρώπων του Πάγου με τους αιώνες, θα βρεθεί μέσα στις δικές της προκλήσεις που θα κάνουν την απεγνωσμένη ανάγκη του Βασιλείου για ειρήνη από αυτό το μέτωπο ακόμα πιο δύσκολη για στην κατόρθωσή του• ενώ ο Ehren, έχοντας δραπετεύσει από τις δυνάμεις των χιτινωδών τεράτων με ένα τρομερό μυστικό, θα προσπαθήσει να βοηθήσει τον Πρώτο Άρχοντα να προετοιμάσουν τις Λεγεώνες ενάντια σε μια εφιαλτική ορδή που έχουν μονάχα ελάχιστες πιθανότητες για να επιβιώσουν.<br /><br />Ωστόσο, με το Βασίλειο της Alera να έρχεται για πρώτη φορά μετά από χίλια χρόνια εναντίων της μεγαλύτερής της απειλής, όταν η βασίλισσα των Vord στείλει τις δυνάμεις της ενάντια των αμυνόμενων Λεγεώνων της Πρωτεύουσας, και μακριά στην πατρίδα των Canim τα ανεξέλεγκτα χιτινώδη τέρατα ξεχυθούν προς τους τελευταίους στεκούμενους επιζώντες, ο Tavi και οι σύντροφοί του, η Amara και ο Bernard, η Isana και η Aria, και ο Ehren και ο Πρώτος Άρχοντας, θα πρέπει να αφήσουν τις διαφορές τους κατά μέρος και να πολεμήσουν αυτή την νέα απειλή πριν όλα χαθούν, γιατί αν δεν καταφέρουν να ξεπεράσουν αυτές τις δυσκολίες, η ίδια τους η επιβίωση θα κρεμαστεί από μια κλωστή.<br /><br />Μπαίνοντας στα τελευταία στάδια των περιπετειών των χαρακτήρων, έχοντας χτίσει από την αρχή ένα επικό ταξίδι γεμάτο θαύματα και μαγεία, ο Jim Butcher - οδηγούμενος από τα γεγονότα του προηγούμενου βιβλίου, το <i>Captain’s Fury</i> - μας πηγαίνει για πρώτη φορά σε ολόκληρη την σειρά στην Canea, την πατρίδα των Canim, φέρνοντας ενώπιόν μας τις μεγάλες πόλεις τους που, χωρισμένες ανάμεσα στους δυνατότερους ηγέτες, έχουν γίνει το κέντρο της εξουσίας τους, τις διαφορετικές κοινωνίες τους, αποτελούμενες από δημιουργούς και τεχνίτες μέχρι και πολεμιστές και τυπολάτρες, και τους κώδικες που ακολουθούν• όπως επίσης και στα βόρεια σύνορα του Βασιλείου, πέρα από το Τοίχος και των αμυνόμενων πόλεών τους, δίνοντάς μας μια ματιά από την πρωτόγονη φυλή των Ανθρώπων του Πάγου, τους λόγους των εχθροπραξιών τους, και τους κανόνες και τα πιστεύω με τα οποία ζουν.<br />Αλλά φέρνοντάς μας συγχρόνως πιο κοντά από ποτέ και μέσα στις κυψέλες των Vord, και τις πανίσχυρες βασίλισσές τους που κυβερνάνε μέσα από το <i>croach</i> - της ζελατινώδης πράσινης ουσίας που μπορεί να καταβροχθίσει οτιδήποτε ζωντανό - που τους δίνουν την δυνατότητα να παράγουν εφιαλτικά πλάσματα σε ταχύτατους ρυθμούς, δημιουργώντας πολεμιστές εξαιρετικά ανώτερης δύναμης και ικανότητας - τρεις φυλές που, ερχόμενες σε αντίθεση με τα φαινομενικά ιδανικά των ανθρώπων της Alera, δείχνουν μαζί με τους βάρβαρους Marat τις τεράστιες διαφορές τους αλλά και το μεγαλείο αυτού του κόσμου.<br /><br />Και, φέρνοντας αυτό το επικό ταξίδι ένα βήμα πιο κοντά προς την ολοκλήρωσή του, ο Butcher μας βυθίζει στο <i>Princeps’ Fury</i> στην μεγαλύτερη απειλή που έχει έρθει στο Βασίλειο της Alera για περισσότερο από χίλια χρόνια, αναμιγνύοντας για άλλη μια φορά την πολιτική με τον πόλεμο, και τις μονομαχίες με τα προσωπικά συμφέροντα, ταξιδεύοντάς μας μέσα από τις δυτικές θάλασσες, το βορρά και τον νότο μέσα σε μια ιστορία διπλωματών, Πολεμάρχων, Υψηλών Αρχόντων, πρωτόγονων άγριων, χιτινωδών τεράτων και εφιαλτικών βασιλισσών, και σε μια περιπέτεια υποδούλωσης, εκμηδένισης, συμβιβασμού, επιβίωσης, και πίστης και αφοσίωσης που δημιουργούν στο τέλος ένα μεγάλο κύμα συναισθημάτων, ανεβάζοντας τις προσδοκίες για το τελικό βιβλίο ακόμη περισσότερο.<br /><br />Εν κατακλείδι, το <i>Princeps’ Fury</i> είναι ένα από τα δυνατότερα βιβλία της σειράς, με τον Jim Butcher - φέρνοντας τις περιπέτειες των χαρακτήρων ένα βήμα πιο κοντά προς την ολοκλήρωσή τους - να μας πηγαίνει μέσα σε ένα νέο, μεγάλο πόλεμο, ταξιδεύοντάς μας μέσα σε μια ιστορία θαλασσοπόρων, Πολεμάρχων, πρωτόγονων κατοίκων του βορρά, και χιτινωδών τεράτων, αλλά και σε μια περιπέτεια εκμηδένισης, συμβιβασμού και αφοσίωσης που αφήνει ωστόσο πολλά ζητήματα ανοιχτά για να λυθούν στο έκτο και τελευταίο βιβλίο. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span></span>
  <a data-text-id="4233690529113725087" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
